Differences Identification: 1. Lord Stevens' definition: Lord Stevens defines collusion as ranging "from the wilful failure to keep records, the absence of accountability, the withholding of intelligence and evidence, through to the extreme of agents being involved in murder." 2. Peter Cory's definition: Peter Cory highlights several dictionary definitions of the word collude, including "to co-operate secretly: to have a secret understanding." He also quotes Webster's dictionary, stating that collusion is "to pretend ignorance or unawareness of something one ought morally, or officially or legally to oppose; to fail to take action against a known wrongdoing or misbehaviour - usually used with connive at the violation of a law." 3. Nuala O'Loan's definition: Nuala O'Loan adopts the definitions of Lord Stevens and Peter Cory to examine whether there had been collusion in the murder of Raymond McCord jnr. 4. Al Hutchinson's definition: Al Hutchinson applies a less broad definition in his report on the attack, in 1971, on McGurk's Bar. 5. Sir Christopher de Silva's definition: Sir Christopher de Silva adopts a "working definition" of collusion less broad than that of Judge Cory and more in line with that of the Billy Wright inquiry panel. 6. Peter Smithwick's definition: Peter Smithwick gives a similar definition of collusion to that of Peter Cory, noting that it should be considered in terms of an omission or failure to act.  Explanation and Rationale: Output (a) and Output (b) both provide a comprehensive summary of the various definitions of collusion provided by different people in the article. However, Output (a) is more detailed and specific in its explanation of each definition, while Output (b) is more concise and condensed.
